Demotic: Gr. (ฮฮทฮผฮฟฯฮนฯฮฟฯ, of or for the common people, popular, democratic; (ฮดฮทฮผฮฟฯฮทฯ) = one of the common people). (the common 
people) Applied specifically to the alphabet used by the laity and people of Egypt after 500 or 600B.C. in contradistinction to 
that used by the priestly caste, which was called Hieratic, and of which it was a simplified form. 

Quet: โAt the time of the ptolemies three languages were were extant in Egypt; the hieroglyphic or dead Egyptian; the demotic or 
vernacular, the spoken language of the day written in a simpler manner by cursive signs on a modified hieroglyphic system, and 
standing in the same relation to it as modern English compared with the dead anglo-saxonโ cooper: Monumental Hist, of Egypt. 1876 
p.89.
